\DoxyCodeLine{2108     \{}
\DoxyCodeLine{2109         \textcolor{comment}{// Evil memory leaks.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2110         \textcolor{comment}{// If an XMLElement (etc) is allocated via NewElement() (etc.)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2111         \textcolor{comment}{// and NOT added to the XMLDocument, what happens?}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2112         \textcolor{comment}{//}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2113         \textcolor{comment}{// Previously (buggy):}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2114         \textcolor{comment}{//      The memory would be free'd when the XMLDocument is}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2115         \textcolor{comment}{//      destructed. But the XMLElement destructor wasn't called, so}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2116         \textcolor{comment}{//      memory allocated for the XMLElement text would not be free'd.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2117         \textcolor{comment}{//      In practice this meant strings allocated for the XMLElement}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2118         \textcolor{comment}{//      text would be leaked. An edge case, but annoying.}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2119         \textcolor{comment}{// Now:}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2120         \textcolor{comment}{//      The XMLElement destructor is called. But the unlinked nodes}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2121         \textcolor{comment}{//      have to be tracked using a list. This has a minor performance}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2122         \textcolor{comment}{//      impact that can become significant if you have a lot of}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2123         \textcolor{comment}{//      unlinked nodes. (But why would you do that?)}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2124         \textcolor{comment}{// The only way to see this bug was in a Visual C++ runtime debug heap}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2125         \textcolor{comment}{// leak tracker. This is compiled in by default on Windows Debug and}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2126         \textcolor{comment}{// enabled with \_CRTDBG\_LEAK\_CHECK\_DF parameter passed to \_CrtSetDbgFlag().}}
\DoxyCodeLine{2127         \{}
\DoxyCodeLine{2128             \mbox{\hyperlink{classtinyxml2_1_1_x_m_l_document}{XMLDocument}} doc;}
